<!-- page 5 -->
Census is not merely a head count but is a reflection of truth and facts as they exist in a country about its people, their diversity of habitation, religion, culture, language, education, health and socio-economic status.

Population is basic to production and distribution of material wealth. In order to plan for and implement economic and social development, administrative activity or scientific research, it is necessary to have a reliable and detailed data on size, distribution and composition of population. Population census is a primary source of these basic benchmark statistics, covering not only the settled population but also the homeless persons and nomadic groups. Census 2011 is the fifteenth census in this continuous series from 1872 and the seventh since independence.

![Portrait of Sachin Sinha, I.A.S.](0e62b4ac2303ba5f3ff10123a7c0f273_img.jpg)

Portrait of Sachin Sinha, I.A.S.

SACHIN SINHA

I.A.S.

It is my great pleasure to present the highlights of final population data of Madhya Pradesh as per Census 2011 in this volume. The data released earlier was the provisional data. The data presented here is the final data about population, child population (in the age group of 0-6 years) scheduled castes and scheduled tribes population, literacy and work status which is based on duration of work (main and marginal) as well as category of work (cultivators, agricultural labourers, household industry workers and other workers). The gender composition and the residence status of each set of data have also been presented at the district level. In all 48 statements, 21 graphs and 21 maps are included in this publication. This would be followed by a series of publication giving similar data at the district level. The data at sub-district (tahsil), town (ward) and village level would be released subsequently in electronic version.

I take this opportunity to place on record my gratitude to Dr. C. Chandramouli, Registrar General and Census Commissioner, India for his active co-operation, constant inspiration, guidance and whole hearted support extended to me from time to time. I also wish to record my sincere thanks to Additional RGIs Mr. Deepak Rastogi and Mr. R.C. Sethi and all the senior officers working in various divisions in the office of Registrar General, India for their support.

The data set presented in this volume has been finalized after vigorous quality, consistency and validation checks. My special appreciation to all the officials of the Directorate of Census Operations Madhya Pradesh including those of Data Processing Division, Census Section, Central Tabulation Unit (CTU), Printing and Map Division.

I hope that data presented in this volume will prove very useful to the state government, planners, administrators and research scholars.

Image: Signature of Sachin Sinha

SACHIN SINHA  
I.A.S.

Bhopal  
20<sup>th</sup> May, 2013

Director of Census Operations,  
Madhya Pradesh, Bhopal

<!-- page 7 -->
## 1. ADMINISTRATIVE UNITS

Census 2011 in Madhya Pradesh covered 50 districts, 342 Sub-districts(Tahsil), 476 Towns (Statutory Towns 364 & Census Towns 112) and 54,903 Villages. In Census 2001, the corresponding figures were 45 Districts, 259 Sub-districts (Tahsil), 394 Towns (Statutory Towns 339 & Census Towns 55) and 55,393 Villages. There has been an increase of 5 Districts, 83 Sub-districts (Tahsil), 83 Towns (Statutory Towns 26 and Census Towns 57) and a decrease of 490 Villages in Census 2011 as compared to Census 2001.

## 2. POPULATION

As per Census 2011, the total population of India at 0.00 hours of 1st March 2011 is 1210.6 million. Of this, the rural population is 833.5 million and the urban population is 377.1 million. In absolute numbers, out of total increase of 182 million in the last decade, the contribution of rural and urban areas is equal (91.0 million each). Uttar Pradesh has the largest share in rural population at 155.3 million (18.6% of the country's rural population) whereas Maharashtra has the highest share in urban population with 50.8 million (13.5% of the country's urban population).

In Madhya Pradesh total population as per Census 2011, at 0.00 hours of 1st March, 2011 is 72.6 million, comprising of 52.6 million rural and 20.1 million urban population. In absolute numbers, out of the total increase of 12.3 million in the last decade, the contribution of rural and urban areas is 8.2 million and 4.1 million respectively. Rewa has the largest share of rural population at 1.97 million (3.7% of the State's rural population) followed by Dhar (3.4%) and Satna (3.3%) whereas Indore has the highest share of urban population at 2.4 million (12.1%) followed by Bhopal (9.6%) and Jabalpur (7.2%).

## 3. GROWTH RATE

The growth rate of population in India during the last decade is 17.7% (Rural-12.3%; Urban - 31.8%). Similarly growth rate of population in Madhya Pradesh between 2001 and 2011 is 20.3% (Rural - 18.4% and Urban - 25.7%).

## 4. DENSITY OF POPULATION (PERSONS PER SQ. KM.)

In India, density of population in Census 2011 is 382 showing an increase of 57 points from 2001. Delhi (11,320) turns out to be the most densely inhabited followed by Chandigarh (9,258), in all States/UTs, both in 2001 and 2011 Census. Among the major States, Bihar occupies the first position with a density (1,106), surpassing West Bengal which occupied the first position during 2001 Census. The minimum density of population is in Arunachal Pradesh (17) for both the Censuses.

In Madhya Pradesh density of population in Census 2011 is 236 which shows an increase of 40 points from the Census 2001 figure of 196. Bhopal (855) turns out to be the most densely populated district followed by Indore (841) and Jabalpur (473). The minimum population density is in Dindori (94) followed by Sheopur (104) and Panna (142).

## 5. PROPORTION OF POPULATION

In terms of percentage in India, the rural population constitutes 68.8% and Urban population 31.2% of the total population. There has been an increase of 3.4% in the proportion of urban population in the last decade. Himachal Pradesh (90.0%) has the largest proportion of rural population, whereas Delhi (97.5%) has the highest proportion of urban population.

<!-- page 8 -->
In Madhya Pradesh, the rural population constitutes 72.4% and urban population 27.6% of the total population. There has been an increase of 1.1% in the proportion of urban population in the last decade. The urban proportion was 26.5% in 2001 Census. Dindori (95.4%) has the largest proportion of rural population, while Bhopal (80.9%) has the highest proportion of urban population.

## **6. SEX RATIO (NUMBER OF FEMALES PER 1,000 MALES)**

The Sex Ratio in the country which was at 933 in 2001 has increased by 10 points to 943 in 2011. In rural areas the sex ratio has increased from 946 to 949. The corresponding increase in urban areas has been of 29 points from 900 to 929. In Census 2011, Kerala has recorded the highest sex ratio with respect to total (1084), rural (1078) and urban population (1091) respectively. The lowest sex ratio in rural areas has been recorded in Chandigarh (690) and the corresponding value in urban areas has been returned in Daman & Diu (551).

The sex ratio in Madhya Pradesh which was 919 in 2001 has increased by 12 points to 931 in 2011. In rural areas the sex ratio has increased from 927 to 936, an increase of 9 points. The corresponding increase in urban areas has been 20 points from 898 to 918. Balaghat has recorded the highest sex ratio in respect to total (1021), rural (1024) and urban population (1000) respectively. In 2001 Census also, Balaghat had recorded the highest sex ratio in respect to total (1022), rural (1030) and urban population (970) respectively. The lowest sex ratio in rural areas has been recorded in Bhind (828). The corresponding value in urban areas has been returned from Morena (858).

## **7. CHILD POPULATION (0-6 YEARS)**

As per Census 2011, in India, the child population in the age group of 0-6 years stands at 164.5 million. Of this, 121.3 million were returned in rural areas and 43.2 million in urban areas. Compared to Census 2001, the Child population has increased by 0.7 million in the country. There has been a decline of 5.2 million in rural areas and an increase of 5.9 million in urban areas. In terms of proportion of child population to the total population, there has been a decline of 2.4 percentage points in rural areas and 1.6 percentage points in urban areas. The growth rate of Child population is 0.4% in the last decade. However, there has been a decline of 4.1% in rural areas and an increase of 15.6% in urban areas.

The child population in the age group 0-6 years in Madhya Pradesh stands at 10.8 million. Of this, 8.3 million were returned in rural areas and 2.5 million, in urban areas. Compared to Census 2001, the child population has increased marginally by 27,181 only during the decade. There has been a decline of 118,013 in rural areas and an increase of 145,194 in urban areas. While looking at gender wise child population (0-6), it is noticed that Male child population has increased by 56,325 whereas, Female child population has decreased by 29,144 during 2001-2011. In terms of proportion of child population to the total population, there has been a decline of 3.2 percentage points in rural areas and 2.2 percentage points in urban areas. The growth rate of Child population is 0.25% in the last decade. However, there has been a decline of 1.4% in rural areas and an increase of 6.2% in urban areas. In 26 districts the child population has declined in 2011 compared to 2001 Census. The maximum decline is in Chhindwara (-26195) followed by Betul (-23452) and Rewa (-22654).

## **8. CHILD SEX RATIO (0-6 YEARS) (GIRLS PER THOUSAND BOYS)**

Census 2011 marks a considerable fall in child sex ratio (0-6 years) from 927 to 919 (-8 points) during 2001-2011 in the country. This is the lowest sex ratio since 1961. In rural areas, the fall has been to the tune of 11 points (934 to 923) and in urban areas, the decline has been by 1 point

<!-- page 9 -->
(906 to 905) over the last decade. Delhi (814) has recorded the lowest and Chhattisgarh (977) the highest child sex ratio in rural areas. Haryana (832) has recorded the lowest and Puducherry (975) the highest child sex ratio in urban areas.

In Madhya Pradesh also, Census 2011 marks a considerable fall in child sex ratio (0-6 years) from 932 to 918 (-14 points) during 2001-2011. This is the lowest child sex ratio since 1981. In rural areas, the fall has been to the tune of 16 points (939 to 923) and in urban areas, the decline has been by 6 points (907 to 901) over the last decade. Morena (829) has recorded the lowest and Alirajpur (978) the highest child sex ratio in rural areas. Morena (829) has recorded the lowest and Dindori (998) the highest child sex ratio in urban areas. Child Sex Ratio (0-6 years) has shown a considerable fall from 932 during Census 2001 to 918 during Census 2011 which is clearly a decline of 14 points

## 9. SCHEDULED CASTE POPULATION

In India proportion of the Scheduled Caste population constitutes 16.6% of the total population in 2011 Census. The proportion during the last Census was 16.2%. Thus there has been an increase of 0.4% during the last decade.

In Madhya Pradesh, the total Scheduled Caste population returned in Census 2011 is 11.3 million. Out of these 8.3 million are in rural areas and 3.1 million in urban areas

- In terms of proportion, the Scheduled Caste population constitutes 15.6% of the total population in the state. The proportion during the last Census was 15.2%. Thus there has been an increase of 0.4% during the last decade.
- The Scheduled Caste population in absolute numbers has increased by 2.2 million. This constitutes a decadal growth of 23.9%.
- In terms of gender composition, there are 5.9 million males (Rural-4.3 million and Urban - 1.6 million) and 5.4 million females (Rural-4.0 million and Urban - 1.5 million).
- The highest proportion of Scheduled Caste population to total population is recorded in Ujjain (26.4%) and the lowest in Jhabua (1.7%).

## 10. SCHEDULED TRIBE POPULATION

In India proportion of the Scheduled Tribe population constitutes 8.6% of the total population in 2011 Census. The proportion during the last Census was 8.2%. There has been an increase of 0.4% during the last decade.

In Madhya Pradesh, the total Scheduled Tribe population returned in Census 2011 is 15.3 million, highest in the country. Of this, 14.3 million are in rural areas and 1.0 million in urban areas.

- In terms of proportion, the Scheduled Tribe population constitutes 21.1% of the total population. The proportion during the last Census was 20.3%. Thus there has been an increase of 0.8% during the last decade.
- The Scheduled Tribe population in absolute numbers has increased by 3.1 million. This constitutes a decadal growth of 25.2%.
- In terms of gender composition, there are 7.7 million male (Rural- 7.2 million and Urban - 0.5 million) and 7.6 million female (Rural -7.1 million and Urban - 0.5 million).
- The highest proportion of Scheduled Tribe population to total population is recorded in Alirajpur (89.0%) and the lowest in Bhind (0.4%).

<!-- page 10 -->
## 11. LITERATES (AGE 7 YEARS AND ABOVE)

- The number of literates in India is 763.5 million in Census 2011. Out of these 482.7 million literates are in rural areas and 280.8 million literates are in urban areas. An increase of 202.8 million literates during the decade 2001-2011, rural areas accounted for 120.8 million and urban areas 82.0 million.

In Madhya Pradesh, the number of literates is 42.9 million. Out of these 28.3 million literates are in rural areas and 14.6 million literates in urban areas. An increase of 11.3 million literates during the decade 2001-2011, rural areas accounted for 7.5 million and urban areas 3.7 million.

- The male literates in India are 434.7 million (56.9% of the total literates). In Madhya Pradesh male literates are 25.2 million (58.7% of the total literates).
- The female literates in India are 328.8 million (43.1% of the total literates). In Madhya Pradesh female literates are 17.7 million. (41.3% of total literates).

## 12. EFFECTIVE LITERACY RATE

- The Effective Literacy Rate in India is 73.0% (Rural- 67.8%; Urban- 84.1%). There has been an increase of 8.2 percentage points (9.1 percentage points in rural areas and 4.2 percentage points in urban areas) during the last decade.

The effective literacy rate in Madhya Pradesh is 69.3% (Rural-63.9%; Urban- 82.8%) marking an increase of 5.6 percentage points (6.1 percentage points in rural areas and 3.4 percentage points in urban areas) during the last decade.

- Male Literacy :** The male Literacy rate in India is 80.9% (Rural-77.2%; Urban-88.8%). The highest male literacy rate in rural areas is returned from Kerala (95.4%), while the lowest is returned from Arunachal Pradesh (67.4%). In urban areas, the lowest male literacy rate is returned from Uttar Pradesh (80.4%) and the highest is in Mizoram (98.0%).

In Madhya Pradesh, the male literacy rate is 78.7% (Rural- 74.7%; urban 88.7%). The highest male literacy rate in rural areas is in Bhind (84.8%), while the lowest is in Alirajpur (37.9%). In urban areas, the lowest male literacy rate is in Tikamgarh (82.2%) and the highest is in Seoni (93.3%).

- Female Literacy :** The female Literacy rate in India is 64.6% (Rural-57.9%; Urban- 79.1%). The highest female literacy rate in rural areas is in Kerala (90.8%), while the lowest is in Rajasthan (45.8%). In urban areas, the lowest female literacy rate is in Jammu & Kashmir (69.0%) and the highest is in Mizoram (97.3%).

In Madhya Pradesh, the female literacy rate is 59.2% (Rural- 52.4%; Urban- 76.5%). The highest female literacy rate in rural areas is in Balaghat (67.1%), while the lowest is in Alirajpur (26.4%). In urban areas, the lowest female literacy rate is in Sheopur (62.3%) and the highest in Seoni (84.3%).

- Growth in Female Literacy :** The female literacy rate in India has increased significantly by 10.9 percentage points in the last decade (Rural - 11.8 percentage points and Urban - 6.2 percentage points). On the other hand, male literacy rate increased only by 5.6 points (Rural- 6.5 percentage points and Urban- 2.5 percentage points). It is significant to note that the gap in literacy rate among males and females has reduced from 21.6 in 2001 to 16.3 in 2011 (Rural- from 24.6 in 2001 to 19.3 in 2011 and Urban from 13.4 in 2001 to 9.7 in 2011).

<!-- page 11 -->
The female literacy rate in Madhya Pradesh has increased significantly by 8.9 percentage points in the last decade (Rural- 9.6 percentage points and Urban- 6.0 percentage points). On the other hand, male literacy rate increased slightly by 2.6 percentage points (Rural- 3.0 percentage points and Urban-1.3 percentage points). It is significant to note that the gap in literacy rate among males and females has reduced from 25.8 in 2001 to 19.5 in 2011 (Rural from 28.9 in 2001 to 22.3 in 2011 and Urban from 16.9 in 2001 to 12.2 in 2011).

## 13. WORKERS

- a. As per Census 2011, the total number of workers in India is 481.7 million. Out of these 331.9 million workers are male and 149.9 million are female. Out of the increase of 79.5 million workers during the decade 2001-2011, male workers have accounted for 56.8 million and female workers 22.7 million.

In Madhya Pradesh the total numbers of workers is 31.6 million. Out of these 20.1 million workers are male and 11.4 million are female. Out of the increase of 5.8 million workers during the decade 2001-2011, male workers have accounted for 4.0 million and female workers for 1.8 million.

- b. In India the workers have registered a growth of 19.8%, which is marginally higher than the overall population growth rate of 17.7% during the decade. The male workers have grown by 20.7% and female workers by 17.8%.

The workers in Madhya Pradesh have registered a growth of 22.4%, which is marginally higher than the overall population growth rate of 20.3% during the decade. The male workers have grown by 24.4% as against the female workers growth of 19.0%.

- c. In India, 348.6 million workers are in the rural areas and 133.1 million, are in the urban areas. The female workers in rural and urban areas are 121.8 and 28.0 million respectively.

In Madhya Pradesh 24.7 million workers are in the rural areas and 6.9 million, are in the urban areas. The female workers in rural & urban areas are 10.0 million and 1.5 million respectively.

## 14. WORK PARTICIPATION RATES

- a. The Work Participation Rate (WPR) for the country is 39.8%. This is marginally higher than the corresponding WPR of 39.1% in Census 2001. The WPR for males has increased to 53.3% in 2011 in comparison to 51.7% in Census 2001. The female WPR has reduced marginally to 25.5% in 2011 from 25.6% in Census 2001.

The work participation rate (WPR) for the state of Madhya Pradesh 43.5%. This is marginally higher than the corresponding WPR of 42.7% in Census 2001. The WPR for males has increased to 53.6% in 2011 in comparison to 51.5% in Census 2001. The female WPR has reduced marginally from 33.2% in 2001 to 32.6% in 2011.

- b. In India, Himachal Pradesh (51.9%) ranks first in WPR for total workers as well as female workers (44.8%). The lowest WPR has been reported from Lakshadweep (29.1%). The lowest female WPR has been reported from NCT of Delhi (10.6%). The highest male WPR has been recorded in Daman & Diu (71.5%) and lowest in Lakshadweep (46.2%).

In Madhya Pradesh, Dindori (55.3%) ranks first in WPR for total workers as well as female workers (52.9%). Bhind (30.6%) reported the lowest WPR for total workers as well as female workers (8.4%). The highest male WPR has been recorded in Mandsaur (58.2%) and lowest in Morena (49.2%).

<!-- page 12 -->
## 15. MAIN AND MARGINAL WORKERS

- a. In India as per Census 2011, out of 481.7 million total workers, 362.4 million are main workers and the remaining 119.3 million are marginal workers. The percentage of main workers among the total workers in Census 2011 is 75.2% against 77.8% in Census 2001.

In Madhya Pradesh, in Census 2011, out of 31.6 million total workers, 22.7 million are main workers and the remaining 8.9 million are marginal workers. The percentage of main workers among the total workers in Census 2011 is 71.9% against 74.1% in Census 2001.

- b. The percentage of main workers among the male workers is 82.3% and female workers is 59.6%. The percentage of male main workers has reduced from 87.3% to 82.3% in Census 2011. On the other hand, the percentage of female main workers has increased from 57.3% to 59.6% in Census 2011. Daman & Diu reported highest percentage of main workers (96.0%) as per Census 2011 and minimum of 52.1% in Jharkhand.

In Madhya Pradesh the percentage of main workers among the male workers is 81.2% and among female workers the corresponding figure is 55.5%. The percentage of male main workers has reduced from 86.8% in 2001 to 81.2% in 2011 on the other hand the percentage of female main workers has increased from 52.6% in 2001 to 55.5% in Census 2011. Indore reported highest percentage of main workers (89.7%) as per Census 2011 and Umaria with minimum at 47.8%.

- c. For the first time in Census 2011, the marginal workers have been sub-divided in two categories, namely, those who work for less than 3 months and those who work for 3 months or more but less than six months. In India amongst the 119.3 million marginal workers, around 97 million worked for 3 to 6 months whereas only 22.3 million worked for less than 3 months, amounting to 81.3% and 18.7% respectively. Percentage share of persons working for 3 to 6 months is slightly higher in urban areas (85.2%) than in rural areas (80.7%), whereas for persons working for less than 3 months, it is higher in rural areas (19.3%) than its counterpart in urban areas (14.8%). Gujarat has reported highest share of marginal workers (89.3%) in the 3 to 6 months category and Nagaland reported the lowest at 60.9%. For persons working for less than 3 months, it is obvious that these states hold the reverse positions.

In Madhya Pradesh, among the 8.9 million marginal workers, around 7.3 million worked for 3 to 6 months whereas only 1.6 million worked for less than 3 months, amounting to 82.4% and 17.6% respectively. Percentage share of persons working for 3 to 6 months is slightly higher in urban areas (84.2%) than in rural areas (82.2%), whereas, the persons working for less than 3 months, it is higher in rural areas (17.8%) than its corresponding figure in urban areas (15.8%). Burhanpur has reported highest percent of marginal workers (88.9%) in the 3 to 6 months category and Umaria reported the lowest (74.1%). For persons working for less than 3 months, it is obvious that these districts hold the reverse positions.

## 16. CATEGORIES OF ECONOMIC ACTIVITIES OF THE WORKERS

- a. The broad categories of economic activities, also known as a four-fold classification of the workers are Cultivators (CL), Agricultural Labourers (AL), working in Household Industries (HHI) and Other Workers (OW). The cultivators and agricultural labourers broadly show the workers engaged in the agricultural sector, except those engaged in plantation activities, which over the Censuses, have been considered as a part of 'other workers'.

<!-- page 13 -->
- b. In India, as per Census 2011, out of 481.7 million total workers, 118.7 million are cultivators and another 144.3 million are agricultural labourers. Thus nearly 55% of the workers are engaged in agricultural activities compared to 58.2% in Census 2001. Out of one-in-two males and two of every three females are engaged in agricultural activities either as cultivator or as agricultural labourer. Of the remaining workers, 18.3 million are in household industries and 200.4 million are other workers.

In Madhya Pradesh as per Census 2011, out of 31.6 million total workers, 9.8 million are cultivators and another 12.2 million are agricultural labourers. Thus nearly 69.8% of the workers are engaged in agricultural activities compared to nearly 71.5% in Census 2001. Therefore, still more than two-thirds of the total working population is engaged in agricultural pursuits either as cultivator or as agricultural labourer. Out of two-in-three males and four of every five females are engaged in agricultural activities either as cultivator or as agricultural labourer. Of the remaining workers, 1.0 million are in household industries and 8.6 million are among other workers.

- c. During the decade 2001-11, in India, the Census results show a fall of about 9 million in cultivators and an increase of about 38 million in agricultural labourers. The household industries have shown an increase of 1.4 million and other workers have increased by nearly 49 million.

In Madhya Pradesh also the same trend is revealed in the decade 2001-11, the Census results show a fall of about 1.2 million in cultivators and an increase of about 4.8 million in agricultural labourers. The household industry workers have shown a marginal fall of 0.7 million and other workers have increased by nearly 2.3 million.

- d. In India, the fall in the number of cultivators, during the decade 2001-11 was less among the male workers. In Census 2011, the number of male cultivators decreased to 82.7 million from 85.4 million in Census 2001. Among the females, the number of cultivators has reduced to 36.0 million in Census 2011 from 41.9 million in Census 2001.

In Madhya Pradesh the fall in the number of cultivators, during the decade 2001-11, was less among the male workers. As per Census 2011, the number of male cultivators decreased to 6.6 million from 6.9 million in Census 2001. Among the females, the number of cultivators has reduced to 3.3 million in Census 2011 from 4.2 million in Census 2001.

- e. Among the States/UTs. Uttar Pradesh has reported the highest numbers in all the categories of workers, with 19.1 million cultivators, 19.9 million agricultural labourers, 3.9 million in household industries and 22.9 million as other workers.

In Madhya Pradesh, the highest number of cultivators is reported in Dhar (385,552) and lowest in Umarkia (65,369). The highest number of Agricultural labourers is reported in Rewa (463,506) and lowest in Alirajpur (73,693). The highest number of household industries is reported in Sagar (140,458) and lowest in Neemuch (4,020). The highest number of other workers is reported in Indore (888,176) and lowest in Alirajpur (32,645).

<!-- page 14 -->
## DEFINITIONS

### DENSITY OF POPULATION

The density of population is defined as the number of persons, living per Sq. Km.

### SEX RATIO

Sex ratio is defined as number of females per 1000 males in the total population. It is expressed as 'number of females per 1000 males'.

$$\text{Sex-ratio} = \frac{\text{Number of females} \times 1000}{\text{Number of males}}$$

#### CHILD SEX RATIO (0-6 YEARS)

Child Sex-ratio (0-6 years) is defined as number of females in age-group 0-6 years per 1000 males in the same age-group in the total population. It is expressed as 'number of female children age (0-6) years per 1000 male children age (0-6) years'.

$$\text{Child Sex Ratio (0-6 years)} = \frac{\text{Number of female children (0-6 age group)} \times 1000}{\text{Number of male children (0-6 age group)}}$$

### LITERATES

A person aged 7 years and above who can both read and write, with understanding, in any language has been taken as literate. A person, who can only read but cannot write, is not literate. It is not necessary that to be treated as literate, a person should have received any formal education or passed any minimum educational standard. Literacy could also have been achieved through adult literacy classes or through any non-formal educational system. People who are blind and can read in Braille will be treated as literates.

### EFFECTIVE LITERACY RATE

Effective Literacy rate of population is defined as the percentage of literate persons aged 7 and above to the total population aged 7 and above.

$$\text{Effective Literacy Rate} = \frac{\text{Number of Literate persons aged 7 and above} \times 100}{\text{Population aged 7 and above}}$$

<!-- page 15 -->
### **WORK**

Work is defined as participation in any economic activity, with or without compensation, wages or profit. Such participation may be physical and/or mental in nature. Work involves not only actual work but also includes effective supervision and direction of work. It even includes part time help or unpaid work on farm, family enterprise or in any other economic activity. All persons engaged in 'work' as defined above are workers.

Reference period for determining a person as worker and non-worker is one year preceding the date of enumeration.

#### **MAIN WORKERS**

Those persons who had worked for 6 months or more during the reference period (i.e. one year preceding the date of enumeration) are termed as Main Workers.

#### **MARGINAL WORKERS**

In Census 2011, marginal workers have been classified into two categories viz.,

- (1) Worked for 3 months or more but less than 6 months, during the reference period.
- (2) Worked for less than 3 months, during the reference period.

### **WORK PARTICIPATION RATE**

Work participation rate is defined as the percentage of total workers (main and marginal) to total population.

$$\text{Work Participation Rate} = \frac{\text{Total workers (Main + Marginal)} \times 100}{\text{Total Population}}$$

###### CENSUS OF INDIA 2011 MADHYA PRADESH POPULATION

2011

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing district-level population for 2011. Districts are color-coded based on population ranges: 2,000,001 and above (dark orange), 1,500,001 - 2,000,000 (light orange), 1,000,001 - 1,500,000 (yellow), and 1,000,000 and below (light green).](a289b64f80c6df506c0c55d553fc4496_img.jpg)

This map displays the population distribution across districts of Madhya Pradesh in 2011. The districts are labeled and categorized into four population groups based on color. The highest population districts (dark orange) include Bhopal, Indore, Jabalpur, Gwalior, and Rewa. The next highest group (light orange) includes Morena, Bhind, Shivpuri, Sagar, Chhindwara, and Balaghat. The third group (yellow) includes Ujjain, Dewas, Hoshangabad, and many others. The lowest population group (light green) includes Sheopur, Datia, Ashoknagar, and Alirajpur.

CENSUS OF INDIA 2011  
MADHYA PRADESH  
DENSITY OF POPULATION

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing population density in 2011. The map is color-coded by district based on population density per square kilometer. Higher density areas (226 and above) are in orange, while lower density areas (175 and below) are in green.](7119b28e39fa3784606bf8b8f44e4f9d_img.jpg)

This map displays the population density of districts in Madhya Pradesh for the year 2011. The districts are categorized into four density ranges: 226 and above (orange), 201-225 (light orange), 176-200 (yellow), and 175 and below (green). The highest density districts include Morena, Bhind, Gwalior, Datia, Rewa, and Singrauli. The lowest density districts include Sheopur, Shivpuri, Tikamgarh, Chhatarpur, Panna, Satna, Sidhi, Damoh, Katni, Umariya, Shahdol, Anuppur, Dindori, Mandla, Balaghat, Seoni, Chhindwara, Betul, Harda, Hoshangabad, Narmda, Khargone (West Nimar), Khandwa (East Nimar), Burhanpur, Barwani, Alirajpur, Dharmapuri, Dhar, Indore, Dewas, Sehore, Raisen, Bhopal, Vidisha, Guna, Ashoknagar, Mandsaur, Neemuch, Ratlam, Ujjain, Shajapur, Rajgarh, and Alirajpur.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing population density in 2011. The map is color-coded by district based on population density per square kilometer. Higher density areas (226 and above) are in orange, while lower density areas (175 and below) are in green.

2001

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing population density in 2001. The map is color-coded by district based on population density per square kilometer. Higher density areas (226 and above) are in orange, while lower density areas (175 and below) are in green.](d04ba66e3c0eccfd8fd2b0d176d3c941_img.jpg)

This map displays the population density of districts in Madhya Pradesh for the year 2001. The districts are categorized into four density ranges: 226 and above (orange), 201-225 (light orange), 176-200 (yellow), and 175 and below (green). The highest density districts include Morena, Bhind, Gwalior, Datia, Rewa, and Singrauli. The lowest density districts include Sheopur, Shivpuri, Tikamgarh, Chhatarpur, Panna, Satna, Sidhi, Damoh, Katni, Umariya, Shahdol, Anuppur, Dindori, Mandla, Balaghat, Seoni, Chhindwara, Betul, Harda, Hoshangabad, Narmda, Khargone (West Nimar), Khandwa (East Nimar), Burhanpur, Barwani, Alirajpur, Dharmapuri, Dhar, Indore, Dewas, Sehore, Raisen, Bhopal, Vidisha, Guna, Ashoknagar, Mandsaur, Neemuch, Ratlam, Ujjain, Shajapur, Rajgarh, and Alirajpur.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing population density in 2001. The map is color-coded by district based on population density per square kilometer. Higher density areas (226 and above) are in orange, while lower density areas (175 and below) are in green.

This map displays the literacy rate of females across the districts of Madhya Pradesh in 2011. The districts are categorized into four color groups based on their literacy percentage: 60.1 and above (light green), 50.1 - 60.0 (yellow), 40.1 - 50.0 (orange), and 40.0 and below (dark orange). Most districts in 2011 fall into the 50.1 - 60.0 and 60.1 and above categories, indicating a significant increase in female literacy over the previous decades.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the literacy rate of females by district in 2011. The map is color-coded based on the percentage of female literates.

1991

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the literacy rate of females by district in 1991. The map is predominantly dark orange, indicating that most districts had literacy rates of 40.0 and below.](76e00cbe074b2ad6b7bef7674e4549fa_img.jpg)

This map shows the female literacy rates in Madhya Pradesh for the year 1991. The vast majority of districts are colored dark orange, indicating that the literacy rate was 40.0 and below for most of the population. Only a few districts show slightly higher rates in orange or yellow.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the literacy rate of females by district in 1991. The map is predominantly dark orange, indicating that most districts had literacy rates of 40.0 and below.

2001

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the literacy rate of females by district in 2001. The map shows a mix of colors, indicating an increase in literacy rates compared to 1991.](4796a88ec9ba4e1db1436e0162f4b270_img.jpg)

This map illustrates the female literacy rates in Madhya Pradesh in 2001. There is a noticeable shift from the 1991 map, with more districts now colored yellow (50.1 - 60.0) and light green (60.1 and above). However, many districts still remain in the orange (40.1 - 50.0) and dark orange (40.0 and below) categories.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the literacy rate of females by district in 2001. The map shows a mix of colors, indicating an increase in literacy rates compared to 1991.

Line chart showing work participation rate by residence (Total, Rural, Urban, R-U Gap) for Madhya Pradesh from 1961 to 2011. The chart shows that the rural work participation rate remained relatively stable around 54-60%, while the urban rate fluctuated between 45.6% and 53.6%. The total rate followed the rural rate closely. The R-U gap decreased from 9.7% in 1961 to 2.6% in 2011.

![Bar chart showing the decadal change in work participation rate for Madhya Pradesh from 1961-71 to 2001-11. The chart shows negative changes for all categories in the 1961-71 and 1981-91 periods, and positive changes in the 1971-81, 1991-01, and 2001-11 periods. The largest positive change was seen in the urban category in the 2001-11 period at 4.2%.](1317a731c28cbecd9ade13006931047f_img.jpg)

| 2001-11     | 2.1   | 1.3   | 4.2   |

Bar chart showing the decadal change in work participation rate for Madhya Pradesh from 1961-71 to 2001-11. The chart shows negative changes for all categories in the 1961-71 and 1981-91 periods, and positive changes in the 1971-81, 1991-01, and 2001-11 periods. The largest positive change was seen in the urban category in the 2001-11 period at 4.2%.

###### CENSUS OF INDIA 2011 MADHYA PRADESH WORK PARTICIPATION RATE (FEMALES)

2011

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing Work Participation Rate (Females) for 2011 by district. The map uses a color scale from orange (15.0 and below) to yellow (25.1-35.0) to green (35.1 and above).](a90f370ac129475af7bb60d26ddc783f_img.jpg)

This map displays the Work Participation Rate (WPR) for females in Madhya Pradesh for the year 2011, categorized by district. The districts are color-coded based on the percentage of female workers to the female population. Higher WPR districts (35.1% and above) include NEEMUCH, MANDSAUR, RATLAM, JHABUA, DHAR, ALIRAJPUR, BARWANI, KHARGONE (WEST NIMAR), KHANDWA (EAST NIMAR), BURHANPUR, BETUL, CHHINDWARA, SEONI, BALAGHAT, MANDLA, DINDORI, ANUPPUR, SHAHDOL, UMARIA, KATNI, JABALPUR, DAMOH, SAGAR, RAISEN, BHOPAL, VIDISHA, ASHOKNAGAR, GUNA, SHIVPURI, SHEOPUR, MORENA, GWALIOR, BHIND, and DATIA. Moderate WPR districts (25.1-35.0%) include CHHATARPUR, PANNA, SATNA, REWA, SIDHI, and SINGRAULI. Lower WPR districts (15.0-25.0%) include DEWAS, HOSHANGABAD, NARSIMHAPUR, and INDORE.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing Work Participation Rate (Females) for 2011 by district. The map uses a color scale from orange (15.0 and below) to yellow (25.1-35.0) to green (35.1 and above).

1991

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing Work Participation Rate (Females) for 1991 by district.](ae55665c63ee1d1a4ad57500963b0a53_img.jpg)

This map displays the Work Participation Rate (WPR) for females in Madhya Pradesh for the year 1991, categorized by district. The color-coding follows the same scale as the 2011 map. In 1991, the districts with the lowest WPR (15.0% and below) were MORENA, GWALIOR, BHIND, and DATIA. Most other districts showed moderate WPR (25.1-35.0%), with some areas in the west and south showing higher rates (35.1% and above).

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing Work Participation Rate (Females) for 1991 by district.

2001

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing Work Participation Rate (Females) for 2001 by district.](e2af7f361488f2eb87a8c10c00dc6f9e_img.jpg)

This map displays the Work Participation Rate (WPR) for females in Madhya Pradesh for the year 2001, categorized by district. The color-coding follows the same scale as the 2011 map. In 2001, the districts with the lowest WPR (15.0% and below) were MORENA, GWALIOR, BHIND, and DATIA. The majority of districts showed moderate WPR (25.1-35.0%), with a significant number of districts in the western and southern parts of the state showing higher rates (35.1% and above).

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing Work Participation Rate (Females) for 2001 by district.

Most districts are in the 70.1 and above category (green), while some districts in the east and south show lower percentages, falling into the 60.0 and below category (orange). Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of main workers by district in 1991. The map is almost entirely green, indicating that the vast majority of districts had 70.1 or above percentage of main workers in 1991. Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of main workers by district in 2001. The map shows a mix of green and yellow districts, indicating a shift in the percentage of main workers compared to 1991, with more districts falling into the 65.1 - 70.0 category.](34cfb1835fdf0d248bc2c4d58956a896_img.jpg)

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of main workers by district in 2011. The map is color-coded based on the percentage of main workers to total workers. Most districts are in the 70.1 and above category (green), while some districts in the east and south show lower percentages, falling into the 60.0 and below category (orange). Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of main workers by district in 1991. The map is almost entirely green, indicating that the vast majority of districts had 70.1 or above percentage of main workers in 1991. Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of main workers by district in 2001. The map shows a mix of green and yellow districts, indicating a shift in the percentage of main workers compared to 1991, with more districts falling into the 65.1 - 70.0 category.

### CENSUS OF INDIA 2011 MADHYA PRADESH PERCENTAGE OF AGRICULTURAL LABOURERS

2011

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of agricultural labourers in 2011 by district.](f88c98ece93f791a5eb0a524ccc85b54_img.jpg)

This map displays the percentage of agricultural labourers to total workers in Madhya Pradesh for the year 2011. The districts are color-coded based on the following percentage ranges:

- 45.1 And Above (Dark Orange):** Rewa, Satna, Sidhi, Singrauli, Katni, Umaria, Shahdol, Anuppur, Dindori, Mandla, Balaghat, Seoni, Chhindwara, Narsimhapur, Betul, Hoshangabad, Raisen, Sehore, Bhopal, Vidisha, Rajgarh, Shajapur, Ujjain, Ratlam, Jhabua, Alirajpur, Dhar, Barwani, Khargone (West Nimar), Burhanpur, Khandwa (East Nimar), Harda, Dewas, Indore.
- 35.1 - 45.0 (Medium Orange):** Panna, Damoh, Sagar, Ashoknagar, Guna, Mandsaur, Neemuch, Sheopur.
- 25.1 - 35.0 (Yellow):** Tikamgarh, Chhatarpur, Datia, Shivpuri, Gwalior, Bhind, Morena.
- 15.1 - 25.0 (Light Green):** Jabalpur.
- 15.0 And Below (Dark Green):** No districts visible in this range for 2011.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of agricultural labourers in 2011 by district.

BOUNDARIES : -

- STATE
- DIVISION
- DISTRICT

Percentage of Agricultural Labourers  
to Total Workers

- 45.1 And Above
- 35.1 - 45.0
- 25.1 - 35.0
- 15.1 - 25.0
- 15.0 And Below

2001

![Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of agricultural labourers in 2001 by district.](4cf8a7db72c1488fc314904e125b395b_img.jpg)

This map displays the percentage of agricultural labourers to total workers in Madhya Pradesh for the year 2001. The distribution shows a significant shift over the decade, with many more districts in 2011 falling into the higher percentage categories (45.1% and above) compared to 2001. In 2001, many districts were in the 25.1-35.0% (yellow) and 35.1-45.0% (medium orange) ranges.

Map of Madhya Pradesh showing the percentage of agricultural labourers in 2001 by district.
